[All primarily denote proximate sequence.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">عَقَبُونَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَقَبُوا مِنْ خَلْفِنَا</foreign>

In the saying in the Kur [xvi. last verse but one], <foreign lang="ar">وَإِنْ عَاقَبْتُمْ فَعَاقِبُوا بِمِثْلِ مَا عُوقِبْتُمٌ بِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And if ye punish, then punish ye with the like of that with which ye have been afflicted,</hi> lit. <hi rend="ital">punished</hi>], the verb first denotes punishment, and is afterwards used for the purpose of assimilation: and similar to this is the saying in the same [xxii. 59], <foreign lang="ar">وَمَنْ عَاقَبَ بِمِثْلِ مَا عُوقِبَ بِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And whoso punisheth with the like of that with which he hath been afflicted,</hi> lit. <hi rend="ital">punished</hi>]. [In like manner,] it is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">أَبْطَلَ النَّفْحَ إِلَّا أَنْ يُضْرَبَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَيُعَاقِبَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He made the kicking</hi> of a beast <hi rend="ital">with the hind leg to be of no account unless it were beaten</hi> by its master, or rider, <hi rend="ital">and retaliated</hi> by kicking another person]; meaning, he made nothing to be incumbent on the master of the beast unless the latter made the kicking to be a consequence of that [i. e. unless the beast kicked in consequence of its being beaten by the master, or rider].                   <foreign lang="ar">عقَب</foreign>; <hi rend="ital">the former being such as incline to yellow, whereas the latter incline to white, and are the harder, and firmer,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stronger, of the two:</hi> AHn says, on the authority of Aboo-Ziyád, that the <foreign lang="ar">عَقَب</foreign> are [the <hi rend="ital">sinews,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tendons,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of the two portions of flesh next the back-bone on either side, of the sheep or goat, and of the camel, and of the ox or cow,</hi>(TA.)       <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29834-1" target="عَقْبٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n29831"/></foreign>, (Msb, TA,) the latter being a contraction of the former, (Msb,) [The <hi rend="ital">heel</hi> of a human being;] the <hi rend="ital">hinder part of the foot</hi> of a human being: (S, Mgh, O, Msb, K:) of the fem. gender: (S, O, Msb:) pl. [of pauc.] <foreign lang="ar">أَعْقُبٌ</foreign> (TA) and [of mult. as well as of pauc.] <foreign lang="ar">أَعْقَابٌ</foreign>: (Msb, TA:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29834-2" target="عَقِيبٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n29848"/></foreign> is said to signify the same; but MF cites an assertion that this is a word of a bad dialect. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">وَيْلٌ لِلْأَعْقَابِ مِنَ النَّارِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Wo to the heels from the fire</hi> of Hell], (O, Msb, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">ويل لِلْعَقِبِ من النّار</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Who to the heel</hi> &amp;c.], (TA,) occurring in a trad., means wo to him who neglects the washing of the heels in the ablution preparatory to prayer. (O, * Msb, TA. *) <foreign lang="ar">عَقِبُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الشَّيْطَانِ</foreign>, (O, Msb, TA,) or, as some say,   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29834-3" target="عُقْبَةُ" n="3" lang="ar" type="7" subtype="WOTF"/> الشيطان</foreign>, (Msb, TA,) with damm, (TA,) which is forbidden in prayer, is expl. as meaning <hi rend="ital">The placing the buttocks upon the heels between the two prostrations;</hi> which is what some term <foreign lang="ar">الإِقْعَآءُ</foreign>: (Mgh, * O, Msb, TA:) so says A'Obeyd: (Msb:) or, accord. to some, this means <hi rend="ital">the leaving the heels unwashed in the ablution preparatory to prayer.</hi> (O.) <foreign lang="ar">وَطِئَ النَّاسُ عَقِبَ فُلَانٍ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">The people trod upon the heel of such a one</hi>] means <hi rend="ital">the people walked after,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">near after, such a one:</hi> and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ مُوَطَّأُ العَقِبِ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He is one whose heel is trodden upon</hi>]: (O, TA; *) because of his having command over people, and their being submissive to him: (O:) the latter phrase means <hi rend="ital">he is one who has many followers:</hi> (A, TA: [see also art. <foreign lang="ar">وطأ</foreign>:]) <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ زَيْدٌ يَطَأُ عَقِبَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَمْرٍو</foreign> primarily signifies <hi rend="ital">Zeyd came putting his foot in the place of the foot</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">heel</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of 'Amr every time that the latter raised his foot.</hi> (Msb.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ أَيْنَ عَقِبُكَ</foreign>, (A, O,) or <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ أَيْنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ عَقِبُكَ</foreign>, (TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">Whence camest thou?</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Whence hast thou come?</hi> (A, O, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ فُلَانٌ عَلَى عَقِبِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Such a one returned by the way of his heel;</hi> i. e., <hi rend="ital">by the way that was behind him,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">whence he had come; quickly.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">وَلَّى عَلَى عَقِبِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى عَقِبَيْهِ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He turned back,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">receded, from a thing to which he had betaken himself.</hi> (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">لَا تَرُدَّهُمْ عَلَى أَعْقَابِهِمْ</foreign>, occurring in a trad., means <hi rend="ital">Turn not thou them back to their former condition</hi> of not emigrating [for the sake of religion]: and <foreign lang="ar">مَا زَالُوا مُرْتَدِّينَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى أَعْقَابِهِمْ</foreign>, in another trad., means <hi rend="ital">They ceased not to return to infidelity:</hi> as though they went back wards. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  The <foreign lang="ar">عَقِب</foreign> of the <foreign lang="ar">نَعْل</foreign> [or sandal] is The <hi rend="ital">part</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">wide strap</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that embraces the heel.</hi> (AO, in an anom. MS. in my possession.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [And <foreign lang="ar">عَقِبُ البَابِ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">The pivot</hi> (generally of wood) <hi rend="ital">at the bottom of the door, turning in a socket in the threshold.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">عَقِبٌ</foreign> and

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29834-12" target="عَاقِبَةٌ" n="12" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar" select="n29853"/></foreign>, (S, O, Msb, K, TA,) which signifies, (S, O, Msb, K,) i. e. as signifying, (TA,) The <hi rend="ital">end;</hi> or the <hi rend="ital">last,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">latter, part</hi> or <hi rend="ital">state;</hi> [but generally as explanatory of this last word, and often as explanatory of <foreign lang="ar">عُقُبٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عُقْبٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عُقْبَى</foreign>, as meaning the <hi rend="ital">consequence,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">result,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">issue;</hi>] of anything: (S, O, Msb, K, TA:) [and the same words, app. with the exception of <foreign lang="ar">عُقْبَى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عَاقِبَةٌ</foreign>, signify also <hi rend="ital">a time,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">state, of subsequence:</hi>] the pl. [of the first four words is <foreign lang="ar">أَعْقَابٌ</foreign>, and] of the last <foreign lang="ar">عَوَاقِبُ</foreign>. (TA.) Hence, (S,) it is said in the Kur [xviii. 42],   
      <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ خَيْرٌ ثَوَابًا وَخَيْرٌ <ref cref="n29834-13" target="عُقُبًا" n="13" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29834-14" target="عُقْبًا" n="14" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> or

(S, O.) And in the same [xci. last verse],   
      <foreign lang="ar">وَلَا يَخَافُ <ref cref="n29834-16" target="عُقْبَاهَا" n="16" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">And He feareth not the consequence thereof.</hi> (Th, TA.)                   <hi rend="ital">May the end to thee be in that which is good;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">may thy case end in good</hi>]. (TA.)                   <hi rend="ital">I came to him after his arrival.</hi> (Lh, TA.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ يَسْتَقِى عَلَى <ref cref="n29834-33" target="عُقْبَةِ" n="33" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>آلِ فُلَانٍ</foreign>

(TA.) The Arabs say, <foreign lang="ar">لَا عَقِبَ لَهُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">There is,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">are, no male offspring remaining to him:</hi> (TA:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَتْ لِفُلَانٍ <ref cref="n29834-39" target="عَاقِبَةٌ" n="39" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n29853"/></foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">There is,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">are, to such a one, no</hi> [<hi rend="ital">remaining</hi>] <hi rend="ital">child,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">children.</hi> (S, O, Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense><foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29834-40" target="عَقْبُ" n="40" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>شَىْءٍ</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">عَقِبُ شَىْءٍ</foreign>] signifies <hi rend="ital">A thing,</hi> whatever it be, <hi rend="ital">that follows, succeeds, comes after,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">takes the place of, a thing;</hi> as the water of a well, and the blowing of the wind, and the flying of the sand-grouse (<foreign lang="ar">القَطَا</foreign>), and the running of a horse. (TA. [See also <foreign lang="ar">عَاقِبٌ</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">عَقِبٌ</foreign>, (IAar, IF, A, Msb,) or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29834-41" target="عَقْبٌ" n="41" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n29831"/></foreign>, (S, K,) or, as As says, each of these, some of the Arabs using the latter form, by way of contraction, (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">A run after another run,</hi> (As, IF, S, Msb, K,) of a horse: (As, IF, S, Msb:) or the <hi rend="ital">last,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">latter, run,</hi> of a horse: (IAar, Msb:) or one says of a courser, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ ذُوْ عَفْوٍ وَعَقِبٍ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">He has a first run, and a subsequent, and more vehement, run:</hi> (A:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29834-42" target="عِقَابٌ" n="42" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n29846"/></foreign> is said in the L to have the first of these meanings: (TA:) or it is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">عَقْبٌ</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">عَقِبٌ</foreign>] as having that meaning: (Ham p. 358:) an ex. of it occurs in the following verse, (Ham, TA,) cited by IAar: (TA:) <quote>

                  <foreign lang="ar">الرواح</foreign> being redundant,)] <hi rend="ital">and drove her on</hi> [by a pursuit] <hi rend="ital">like the seeking of him who is making repeated efforts, having been wronged, to obtain his due:</hi> (O:) <foreign lang="ar">المظلوم</foreign> is an epithet qualifying <foreign lang="ar">المعقّب</foreign>, and is in the nom. case agreeable with the meaning, (S, O,) because it is put after its proper place; (O;) and <foreign lang="ar">المعقّب</foreign> is literally in the gen. case, but as to the meaning is an agent: (S, O: *) or, accord. to some, <foreign lang="ar">المعقّب</foreign> [here] signifies <hi rend="ital">the debtor who puts off the payment of his debt;</hi> so that <foreign lang="ar">المظلوم</foreign> is an agent and <foreign lang="ar">المعقّب</foreign> is an objective complement: (S:) or, as some say, <foreign lang="ar">المعقّب</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">he who demands the payment of a debt and repeats his demand thereof.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  Also Any one <hi rend="ital">returning</hi> [app. to the doing of a thing]. (O.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">مَعَاقِبٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">لَا مُعَقِّبَ لِحُكْمِهِ</foreign>, in the Kur [xiii. 41], means <hi rend="ital">There is no repeller of his decree.</hi> (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  Also A man <hi rend="ital">who descends into a well to raise a stone of the kind called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عُقَاب</foreign>. (TA.) [See also the verb.]    </entryFree>3c:T99d,<entryFree id="n29862" key="مُعَاقِبٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مُعَاقِبٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>: see <foreign lang="ar">عُقِيبٌ</foreign>, with which it is syn.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">إِبِلٌ مُعَاقِبَةٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Camels that eat one time,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">turn, of the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">kind of plants called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">حَمْض</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">and another of the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">kind called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">خُلَّة</foreign>.                   <hi rend="ital">A palm-tree that bears fruit one year, and fails to do so another.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">مُعَاقِبٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">A revenger of blood:</hi> a poet, cited by IAar, says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَنَحْنُ قَتَلْنَا بِالمَحَارِقِ فَارِسًا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">جَزَآءَ العُطَاسِ لَا يَمُوتُ المُعَاقِبُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> meaning [<hi rend="ital">And we slew, in El-Mahárik,</hi> (app. the name of a place,) <hi rend="ital">a horseman,</hi>] taking our bloodrevenge quickly, <hi rend="ital">in the time that elapses between a sneeze and the prayer for the sneezer</hi> [which is usually “ God have mercy on thee ”]: the memory of <hi rend="ital">the blood-revenger shall not die.</hi> (TA. [It is there also said that <foreign lang="ar">العقب</foreign> (app. a mistranscription for   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n29862-1" target="المُعَقِّبُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, as may be conjectured from the fact that the <foreign lang="ar">م</foreign> after the article is often indistinctly written, and inferred on other grounds,) is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">المُعَاقِبُ</foreign> as here explained.])    </entryFree>3d:T1017,<entryFree id="n29866" key="يَعْقُوبٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">يَعْقُوبٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, perfectly decl., because it is an Arabic word, not altered, and, although having an augmentative letter at the beginning, not of the measure of a verb; whereas <foreign lang="ar">يعقوب</foreign> as a proper name of foreign origin is imperfectly decl.; (S, O;) The <foreign lang="ar">حَجَل</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">partridge</hi>]: (K:) or the <hi rend="ital">male of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَجَل</foreign>; (S, O, Msb;) or <hi rend="ital">of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَبْج</foreign>; (Lh, Mgh;) but ISd says, I know not whether Lh mean by this the <foreign lang="ar">حَجَل</foreign> or the <foreign lang="ar">قَطَا</foreign> or the <foreign lang="ar">كَرَوَان</foreign>, nor do I know that the <foreign lang="ar">قَبْح</foreign> is the same as the <foreign lang="ar">حَجَل</foreign>: (TA:) and the <hi rend="ital">male of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَطَا</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">sand-grouse</hi>]: (TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">يَعَاقِيبُ</foreign>. (S, Mgh, O, Msb.) <foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّكُمْ يَعَاقِيبُ الحَجَلِ</foreign>, occurring in a trad., means [<hi rend="ital">As though ye were the males of partridges</hi>] in your haste, and your flying into destruction: for they are such that, when they see the female in the possession of the fowler, they throw themselves upon him, so as to fall into his hand. (Z, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">ركب</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And accord. to some, (TA,) the pl. also signifies <hi rend="ital">Horses:</hi> they being thus termed as being likened to the <foreign lang="ar">يعاقيب</foreign> of the <foreign lang="ar">حَجَل</foreign>, (O, TA,) because of their swiftness: (TA:) so in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">رَكْضَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">اليَعَاقِيبِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">As the running of the horses,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of the swift horses</hi>]; in a verse of Selámeh Ibn-Jendel: (O, TA:) but others say that the meaning [here] is, <hi rend="ital">the males of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَجَل</foreign>. (TA.) It is said in the L that <foreign lang="ar">فَرَسٌ يَعْقُوبٌ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">A horse that has a run after another run</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">the power of repeating his running</hi>] (<foreign lang="ar">ذُو عَقْبٍ</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">عَقِبٍ</foreign>]). (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  J has cited [in the S] the words of a poet, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">عَالٍ يُقَصِّرُ دُونَهُ اليَعْقُوبُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">High,</hi> so that <hi rend="ital">the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يعقوب</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">falls short of reaching it</hi>] as an ex. of the last word meaning <hi rend="ital">the male of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَجَل</foreign>: but IB says that it appears to mean in this case <hi rend="ital">the male of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عُقَاب</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">eagle</hi>]; like as <foreign lang="ar">اليَرْخُومُ</foreign> means the male of the <foreign lang="ar">رَخَم</foreign>; and <foreign lang="ar">اليَحْبُورُ</foreign>, the male of the <foreign lang="ar">حُبَارَى</foreign>; for the <foreign lang="ar">حَجَل</foreign> is not known to have so high a flight: and ElFarezdak describes <foreign lang="ar">يَعَاقِيب</foreign> as congregating with vultures over the slain.
